I would like to share the link but I have to paste it in the whole PDF file sorry. ToGoGo — Claude Code Master Build Prompt ToGoGo MASTER BUILD PROMPT FOR CLAUDE CODE A Complete PWA Dropshipping & Marketplace Platform Trade · Swap · Connect · Share Version 1.0 — For Claude Code SECTION 1: PROJECT OVERVIEW & VISION You are Claude Code. Your job is to build ToGoGo — a full-stack Progressive Web App (PWA) that democratises dropshipping and peer-to-peer marketplace trading. This app must work seamlessly on iPhone, Android, and desktop PC browsers with no app store install required. The core mission of ToGoGo is to remove unnecessary middlemen from the consumer supply chain, connecting buyers directly with sellers, dropshippers with suppliers, and everyday people with the best global deals — delivered to their door. This document is your complete specification. Build everything described here. Do not skip any section. Prioritise user-friendliness above all — assume the user has minimal technical knowledge. Every interaction must be simple, obvious, and beautiful. 1.1 What ToGoGo Does ToGoGo is three things in one platform: A MARKETPLACE — where people buy, sell, swap, and trade products. A DROPSHIPPING PLATFORM — where anyone can start a dropshipping business without stock, warehousing, or upfront investment. A COMMUNITY CONNECTOR — linking buyers with sellers, suppliers with dropshippers, and people with deals they would never find alone. 1.2 User Types • BUYER — browses and purchases products at the best available price • SELLER — lists products for sale, manages inventory and orders • DROPSHIPPER — curates products from suppliers and sells without holding stock • SUPPLIER — lists wholesale products available for dropshipping • SWAPPER — trades items peer-to-peer with other users • ADMIN — monitors backend, manages users, products, finances, disputes SECTION 2: TECH STACK & ARCHITECTURE 2.1 Frontend • React 18 with Vite for fast builds and hot reload • Tailwind CSS for all styling — clean, responsive, mobile-first • PWA manifest + Service Worker for offline support, home screen install on iPhone and Android • React Router v6 for navigation • Zustand for global state management • React Query (TanStack) for data fetching and caching 2.2 Backend • Node.js with Express.js REST API • PostgreSQL (via Supabase — free tier available) for database • Supabase Auth for authentication (email, Google, Apple Sign In) • Supabase Storage for product images and user uploads • Redis (Upstash free tier) for caching hot products and sessions • Node-cron for scheduled tasks (order sync, price updates, notifications) 2.3 Deployment • Frontend: Vercel (free tier, auto-deploy from GitHub) • Backend API: Railway.app or Render.com (free tier available) • Database: Supabase (free tier, 500MB) • Domain: togogo.app or togogo.co via Namecheap or Cloudflare • SSL: Auto-provisioned by Vercel and Railway SECTION 3: COMPLETE FEATURE LIST 3.1 Onboarding & Account System Build a dead-simple onboarding flow. The first screen must say: 'What do you want to do?' with three big colourful buttons: BUY, SELL, and BOTH. This sets their initial user role. They can change it later. 4. Sign up via email (with verification link) or Google/Apple SSO 5. Profile wizard: name, photo, location (suburb/city only — never full address), short bio, what they sell or look for 6. Identity verification tier system: Level 1 (email), Level 2 (phone SMS), Level 3 (ID upload via Stripe Identity) 7. User trust score displayed on profile (calculated from reviews, sales history, verification level) 8. Seller onboarding connects their payment account (Stripe Connect Express — guided step-by-step) 3.2 Product Discovery & Browsing This is the heart of the app. Every person who opens ToGoGo should immediately see great deals without needing to search. Build smart, beautiful browsing. • Home feed: personalised grid of products based on browsing history and location • Category tiles: Electronics, Fashion, Home, Garden, Sports, Toys, Health, Automotive, Books, Food • Search with instant suggestions, spell correction, and filters (price range, location, condition, shipping speed) • Price comparison: when viewing a product, show the same or similar product from other sellers side-by-side • 'Best Deal' badge automatically applied to the cheapest listing of identical products • Trending now section: algorithmically ranked by views + sales velocity in last 24 hours • Swap section: dedicated tab for peer-to-peer trades, user posts item and what they want in return 3.3 Product Listing (For Sellers & Dropshippers) Listing a product must take less than 2 minutes. Build an intelligent listing wizard. 9. Step 1: Take or upload photos (up to 10). AI auto-removes background and enhances image quality. 10. Step 2: AI suggests title, description, category, and price based on the photos (call Claude API for this). 11. Step 3: User confirms or edits the AI suggestion. Add condition (New/Like New/Good/Fair). 12. Step 4: Set price, quantity, shipping options (local pickup, standard post, express, flat rate). 13. Step 5: One tap to publish. Product goes live immediately. For DROPSHIPPERS: Add a special 'Import from Supplier' mode where they enter an AliExpress, CJ Dropshipping, or Zendrop product URL and the system auto-imports title, images, description, and supplier price, then lets the dropshipper set their markup. 3.4 Dropshipping Engine This is a key differentiator of ToGoGo. Build a complete dropshipping workflow. Supplier Integrations (use their free APIs or web scraping where APIs unavailable): • AliExpress Affiliate API — search products, get pricing, place orders • CJ Dropshipping API — free account, excellent AU/US shipping times • Zendrop API — US-based products, fast shipping, white-label packaging • Spocket — AU and US suppliers with 2-7 day shipping • Manual supplier — seller can add any supplier with manual order processing Dropship Order Flow: 14. Customer places order and pays ToGoGo 15. System automatically places order with supplier using dropshipper's pre-stored supplier account credentials 16. Supplier ships directly to customer — customer's address is used, seller's branding on packing slip if available 17. Tracking number auto-imported and sent to customer via SMS and email 18. Profit (sale price minus supplier cost minus platform fee) auto-deposited to seller's Stripe Connect account within 3 days of delivery confirmation Profit Calculator (built into every product listing for sellers): Show a live widget: Supplier Cost + Shipping + ToGoGo Fee (8%) = Total Cost. Set your price = Your Profit. Profit margin %. This must update in real time as the seller types. 3.5 Payment System Use Stripe as the primary payment processor. It handles all regulatory compliance, fraud detection, and international payments. Do not build custom payment infrastructure. Buyer Payments: • Credit/debit card (Stripe Elements — beautiful embedded card form) • Apple Pay and Google Pay (Stripe Payment Request Button — one tap checkout) • Buy Now Pay Later via Stripe's Afterpay/Clearpay integration • Saved cards for returning customers • ToGoGo Wallet — users can hold a balance and spend it on platform Seller Payouts: • Stripe Connect Express — sellers onboard in 5 minutes, KYC handled by Stripe • Automatic payout schedule: weekly by default, daily available for high-volume sellers • Platform fee: 8% of sale price, deducted before payout • Dispute and refund management handled through Stripe dashboard, surfaced in ToGoGo admin panel Checkout Flow (must be 3 steps maximum): 19. Review cart (product, quantity, shipping method, estimated delivery) 20. Enter/confirm shipping address 21. Pay (Apple Pay appears first on iPhone, Google Pay on Android, card form below) After payment: animated success screen with order number, estimated delivery date, and 'Track my order' button. 3.6 Messaging & Negotiation System • In-app chat between buyer and seller, threaded by listing • Make an Offer button on every listing — buyer proposes price, seller accepts/counters/declines • Offer accepted = payment link auto-generated and sent in chat • Photo sharing in chat (for condition verification, custom order confirmation) • Push notifications for new messages (use web push via Firebase Cloud Messaging) • Auto-translate messages for international buyers/sellers (DeepL free API) 3.7 Reviews & Trust System • Star ratings (1-5) and written review after every completed transaction • Seller response to review allowed within 7 days • Trust Score: calculated from avg rating × (1 + verified transactions / 10), capped at 100 • Top Seller badge unlocked at 50 sales and 4.8+ average rating • Report abuse system with AI pre-screening (call Claude API to classify reported content) 3.8 Shipping & Logistics • Australia Post API integration: auto-calculate postage for AU domestic • Sendle API: cheaper than AusPost for parcels, integrated as alternative • EasyPost API (US/international): unified API for USPS, UPS, FedEx, DHL • Auto-generate printable shipping labels from within the app • Shipment tracking: pull status updates every 4 hours, push to buyer via notification • Flat rate shipping presets for simple sellers: $5 small, $10 medium, $20 large, or free SECTION 4: ADMIN BACKEND DASHBOARD Build a separate /admin route with its own login, accessible only to accounts with admin role in the database. This dashboard is the nerve centre of ToGoGo. It must show real-time data and allow management of every part of the platform. 4.1 Dashboard Overview Page • Live counters: Total Users, Active Listings, Orders Today, Revenue Today, Disputes Open • Revenue chart: daily/weekly/monthly toggle, line graph with Recharts • New user signups graph (last 30 days) • Top selling products table (rank, name, units sold, revenue) • Top sellers leaderboard • Recent orders feed (live, auto-refreshing every 30 seconds) 4.2 User Management • Search and filter all users by name, email, role, trust score, join date, location • View any user's full profile: listings, orders bought, orders sold, reviews given, reviews received, wallet balance • Actions: suspend account, ban account, send warning, manually adjust trust score, force verify, issue refund • Verification queue: list of users who submitted ID for Level 3 verification, approve/reject with one click 4.3 Product & Listing Management • All listings table: search, filter by category/status/seller/price • Reported listings queue: view flagged products, approve/remove/warn seller • Banned items list: admin can add keywords or categories that are auto-rejected on listing creation • Feature a product: admin can promote listings to homepage banner 4.4 Order & Financial Management • All orders table with full detail drill-down: buyer, seller, product, status, timeline, payment status • Dispute management: open/in-review/resolved, admin can message both parties and issue resolution • Financial ledger: every platform fee collected, every payout made, running balance • Refund tool: issue full or partial refund, source from platform fee buffer or clawback from seller payout • Export any table to CSV with one click 4.5 Marketing & Promotions Tools • Send push notification to all users, or segmented (buyers only, sellers only, by location) • Email campaign manager: write and send broadcast email to user segments via SendGrid free tier • Promo code generator: create codes for % discount or $ off, set expiry and max uses • Homepage banner manager: upload image + link for promotional banners, set active/inactive SECTION 5: DROPSHIPPING INTELLIGENCE FEATURES These features are what make ToGoGo smarter than any other dropshipping tool. They are powered by the Claude API and web integrations. 5.1 AI Product Research Assistant Build a dedicated 'Research' tab in the app. When a dropshipper wants to find hot products to sell, they open this tab and get AI-powered research. • Trending Products Feed: pull from Google Trends API (free), TikTok trending hashtags, and AliExpress best sellers. Display in a card format with estimated profit margins. • AI Niche Analyser: user types a product idea, Claude API evaluates demand, competition, profit potential, and seasonal trends, returns a written report with a score out of 10. • Price Spy: user enters a product name, system finds it on AliExpress, Amazon AU, eBay AU, and Kogan, returns a price comparison table so they know the best supplier and the market selling price. • Winning Product Alerts: user can subscribe to product categories and get daily email/push alerts when a new product is trending. 5.2 AI Listing Optimiser After a product is listed, provide a 'Boost My Listing' button that sends the listing to Claude API with this instruction: Rewrite this product title and description to maximise conversion on a marketplace. Make it compelling, include search keywords, and write it at a reading level suitable for all ages. Return the improved version. Display the original vs improved side by side, let the seller accept with one tap. 5.3 Smart Pricing Engine • Auto-reprice: seller sets min and max price, system monitors competitor listings and adjusts price automatically to stay competitive while protecting minimum margin • Demand-based pricing: price increases slightly when a product has many views and low stock • Bundle pricing: suggest to seller when 2+ related products could be bundled for higher average order value 5.4 Best Supplier Finder When a dropshipper imports or searches for a product, automatically query multiple supplier APIs and return a comparison: Supplier name, Unit cost, Shipping cost to Australia, Estimated delivery days, Minimum order quantity, Supplier rating, and a ToGoGo Recommended badge on the best overall option. SECTION 6: MARKETING INTEGRATIONS ToGoGo should help sellers market their products outside the platform too. Build these integrations. 6.1 Social Sharing • Every listing has a Share button that generates a beautiful preview card (Open Graph meta tags) and share links for Facebook, Instagram, TikTok, WhatsApp, and copy link • Auto-generate a square product image optimised for Instagram from the listing photos • Story format (vertical 9:16) image for Instagram/TikTok stories 6.2 Seller Storefront Every seller gets a public URL: togogo.app/store/[username]. This is a beautiful mini-store page showing their listings, trust score, reviews, and a Follow button. This can be shared as a standalone link — perfect for sellers promoting on social media. 6.3 Affiliate Program • Referral links: every user gets a unique referral code. When someone signs up via their link and makes a first purchase, referrer gets $5 credit. • Affiliate dashboard: shows clicks, signups, earnings from referrals • Product affiliate links: any user can share a trackable link to any product and earn 2% of sale if someone buys via their link SECTION 7: UI/UX DESIGN REQUIREMENTS The design must be beautiful, modern, and instantly understood by someone who has never used a marketplace app. Study the best of Gumtree, eBay, and Shopify and make something better. 7.1 Design System • Primary colour: #FF6B35 (orange — ToGoGo brand) • Secondary colour: #06D6A0 (teal — success, trust, eco) • Accent: #FFD23F (yellow — alerts, highlights, badges) • Background: #FAFAFA light mode, #0f0f0f dark mode • Font: Nunito for body text (friendly, rounded, readable). Baloo 2 for headings and logo. • Border radius: 16px for cards, 12px for buttons, 8px for inputs • Shadows: subtle, warm. box-shadow: 0 4px 20px rgba(255,107,53,0.1) • Dark mode toggle in settings, remembers preference 7.2 Mobile Navigation Bottom tab bar (mobile) with 5 tabs: Home (house icon), Search (magnifying glass), Sell (large + button in brand orange, slightly elevated), Inbox (chat bubble with unread badge), and Profile (avatar). This is the standard pattern for mobile marketplaces and must be used. 7.3 Desktop Navigation Left sidebar on desktop (1024px+) with the same 5 sections plus Admin link (if admin role). Top header with search bar, notifications bell, and cart icon. 7.4 Accessibility Requirements • All buttons minimum 44x44px tap target • All images have alt text (AI-generated from listing description) • Colour contrast minimum WCAG AA standard • All forms usable with keyboard only • Loading skeletons instead of spinners for better perceived performance • Error messages must be human-readable: never show raw API errors to users SECTION 8: DATABASE SCHEMA Create the following tables in Supabase PostgreSQL. Enable Row Level Security (RLS) on all tables. Core Tables • users: id, email, name, avatar_url, bio, location_suburb, location_country, role (buyer/seller/both/admin), trust_score, stripe_account_id, wallet_balance, verification_level, created_at • products: id, seller_id (fk users), title, description, price, original_price, condition, category, images (array), quantity, status (active/sold/draft/removed), is_dropship, supplier_id, supplier_cost, shipping_type, location, views_count, created_at, updated_at • orders: id, buyer_id, seller_id, product_id, quantity, unit_price, total_price, platform_fee, seller_payout, status (pending/paid/shipped/delivered/disputed/refunded), shipping_address, tracking_number, supplier_order_id, created_at, updated_at • messages: id, conversation_id, sender_id, content, image_url, offer_price, offer_status, created_at • reviews: id, order_id, reviewer_id, reviewed_id, rating (1-5), body, seller_response, created_at • suppliers: id, name, api_type (aliexpress/cj/zendrop/spocket/manual), api_key_encrypted, base_shipping_cost, avg_delivery_days, is_active • disputes: id, order_id, opened_by, reason, status, admin_note, resolution, created_at • promo_codes: id, code, type (percent/fixed), value, max_uses, uses_count, expires_at, is_active • referrals: id, referrer_id, referred_id, code, status (pending/completed), reward_paid, created_at • notifications: id, user_id, type, title, body, is_read, link, created_at SECTION 9: SECURITY & COMPLIANCE • All API keys stored as environment variables, never in code or client-side • Stripe handles all payment data — ToGoGo never touches raw card numbers • Passwords hashed with bcrypt (Supabase Auth handles this automatically) • Rate limiting on all API endpoints: 100 requests/minute per IP • Input sanitisation on all user-submitted text to prevent XSS and SQL injection • Supabase RLS policies: users can only read/write their own records, public read on active products only • GDPR/Australian Privacy Act compliance: privacy policy page, delete my account function removes all PII • AI content moderation on product listings (call Claude API to check for prohibited items before going live) SECTION 10: BUILD ORDER FOR CLAUDE CODE Build in this exact order. Complete each phase before moving to the next. Each phase must be functional and testable. PHASE 1 — Foundation: Project scaffold (Vite + React + Tailwind + PWA manifest), Supabase project setup, database schema creation, Supabase Auth (email + Google), basic routing, design system (colours, fonts, components), responsive shell layout with bottom nav PHASE 2 — Core Marketplace: Product listing CRUD, image upload to Supabase Storage, product browsing/search, product detail page, user profiles, seller storefront page PHASE 3 — Transactions: Stripe integration (Stripe Connect, Elements, Apple/Google Pay), checkout flow, order creation, basic order management for buyer and seller PHASE 4 — Dropshipping Engine: Supplier API integrations (CJ Dropshipping first as it has the best free API), import product flow, profit calculator, auto order placement PHASE 5 — Communication: In-app messaging, make an offer system, push notifications via FCM, email notifications via SendGrid PHASE 6 — Intelligence: Claude API integrations (AI listing assistant, niche analyser, content moderation), smart pricing engine, shipping integrations (Australia Post, Sendle) PHASE 7 — Admin Dashboard: Full /admin panel with all management features, analytics charts, financial ledger PHASE 8 — Marketing: Social sharing, affiliate program, promo codes, email campaigns, referral system PHASE 9 — Polish & Launch: Full mobile testing on iPhone and Android, performance audit (Lighthouse score 90+), PWA install flow testing, accessibility audit, security review, deployment to Vercel + Railway SECTION 11: ENVIRONMENT VARIABLES NEEDED Before beginning, gather these API keys. Here's the full summary: ToGoGo — Dropshipping Knowledge Base & Strategy The Business Model Dropshipping = you sell, supplier ships. Customer buys from your store → order forwarded to supplier → supplier ships directly to customer. You never touch inventory. Your profit = retail price - wholesale cost - operating costs. Market size: $476B in 2026, projected $1.25 trillion by 2030 (22% CAGR). The opportunity is massive. The Standard Workflow (What Everyone Does) Step Action 1 Find winning products — Google Trends, TikTok trending, AliExpress hot items 2 Import to store — one-click import with images, descriptions, variants 3 Set prices — 2x-3x markup, psychological pricing (.99/.97) 4 Customer orders — pays retail price on your store 5 Auto-forward to supplier — order + shipping address sent automatically 6 Supplier ships direct — picks, packs, ships to customer 7 Tracking syncs back — customer gets tracking email/SMS 8 Handle returns — you own the customer relationship What World-Class Platforms Do DSers (replaced Oberlo): Bulk order processing, saves 96.7% ordering time, multi-store management, backup supplier finder Spocket: US/EU suppliers for 3-7 day delivery, branded invoicing, quality-vetted suppliers CJDropshipping: Free API, 500K+ products, global warehouses (including US), quality inspection, custom packaging AutoDS: AI-powered product research, automated price/stock monitoring across 25+ suppliers Best Practices (World Standard) Supplier Vetting — 84% of dropshippers say this is their #1 challenge Always order samples first Maintain 2-3 backup suppliers per product Check ratings, response times, shipping reliability Pricing Strategy 2x-3x markup standard Build in 5-15% buffer for returns Bundle products to increase average order value Free shipping threshold to increase cart size Shipping — #1 customer complaint Use domestic/regional warehouses when possible (3-7 days) Be transparent about delivery times Offer multiple shipping tiers Proactive tracking updates Customer Service Respond within 24 hours (ideally 4 hours) For low-cost items, refund without requiring return (cheaper than reverse logistics) AI chatbots handle 80% of common queries Common Problems & Solutions Problem Solution Long shipping (15-30 days) Use US/EU warehouses, stock best-sellers with 3PL Quality control Order samples, use suppliers with inspection services Thin margins High-ticket items ($200+), build brand, reduce ad dependency Competition Niche down, brand building, private labeling Supplier goes out of stock Backup suppliers, auto-fallback routing Supplier APIs Available (For ToGoGo) API Free? Full Lifecycle? Best For CJ Dropshipping Yes Yes (products + orders + tracking) Best overall — recommended first integration AliExpress (RapidAPI) Freemium Read-only Product search & data Printful/Printify Yes Yes Print-on-demand segment DummyJSON Yes Mock only Development/testing Amazon Deprecated April 2026 Avoid — Temu No API exists Not viable — What Makes ToGoGo Different (The Vision) Mobile-first — existing platforms are desktop-first. 6 billion people access internet primarily via phone Zero-to-store in 30 minutes — guided onboarding for complete beginners AI-powered — product recommendations, pricing optimization, auto-generated marketing Global by default — multi-language, multi-currency, regional payment methods (M-Pesa, PIX, UPI, etc.) Revenue-share over subscriptions — seller succeeds = platform succeeds End-to-end — store builder + supplier connector + marketing tools, all in one Education integrated — contextual guidance woven into every workflow, not a separate knowledge base Recommended Development Phases Phase What to Build Phase 1 Integrate CJ Dropshipping API — real product browsing, search, prices, images Phase 2 Product import to store — one-click add, pricing rules, inventory sync Phase 3 Order automation — customer order → auto-forward to supplier Phase 4 Tracking & fulfillment — sync tracking numbers, status updates Phase 5 Analytics dashboard — profit tracking, best sellers, margin analysis Phase 6 Marketing tools — AI-generated listings, social media templates Phase 7 Multi-language/currency — global expansion My recommendation: Start with Phase 1 — CJ Dropshipping API integration. It's free, full-lifecycle, 500K+ products, and will give ToGoGo real product data immediately. Read and analyzed Vite configuration file Read and analyzed Vite configuration file
I found it. The root cause of ALL padding issues across the entire app. In index.css line 33-37:
* { margin: 0; padding: 0; box-sizing: border-box; }
This is unlayered CSS. Tailwind CSS 4 uses CSS cascade layers (@layer). In the cascade, unlayered styles ALWAYS beat layered styles. So * { padding: 0 } overrides every single Tailwind padding class (px-4, px-6, py-4, etc.) across the entire app. The homepage works because it uses inline styles which always win. Every other page uses Tailwind classes and gets zeroed out. The fix: Remove this rule. Tailwind 4's built-in preflight already handles the reset properly within its cascade layers.
Removed universal CSS reset rules from stylesheet Removed universal CSS reset rules from stylesheet

That's the correct structure. Let me commit and push this critical fix.

Pushed. This single fix should resolve the padding on every page — Auth, Browse, Watchlist, Shipping, Marketing, Header, everything. What was happening: Your index.css had * { margin: 0; padding: 0; } which is unlayered CSS. Tailwind CSS 4 puts all its utilities inside CSS cascade layers. In the CSS cascade, unlayered styles always override layered styles. So every Tailwind padding and margin class (px-4, px-6, py-4, mb-8, etc.) was being silently zeroed out across the entire app. The homepage was the only page that worked because it uses inline style attributes, which always win regardless of cascade layers. Once Vercel deploys, all pages should have proper spacing. Yes, 100%. This is exactly how platforms like DSers and Oberlo worked before Shopify absorbed them. Here's the model: ToGoGo holds the master API keys. Users never touch an API in their life. User (taps "sell this") → ToGoGo Backend (your master API keys) → CJ Dropshipping API (products, orders) → Printful API (print-on-demand) → AliExpress API (catalog) → Shopify/WooCommerce API (pushes listing to THEIR store)
How it works for the user: They browse products in ToGoGo (pulled via YOUR master keys) They tap "Sell This" They connect their Shopify/WooCommerce store once (OAuth - just "Allow" button) ToGoGo pushes the product listing, images, description, and price to their store automatically When someone buys from their store, ToGoGo catches the webhook and auto-orders from the supplier Supplier ships direct to the buyer The user literally never: Signs up for a supplier account Copies product descriptions Handles shipping Manages inventory What you need on the backend: Master/Partner API accounts with CJ Dropshipping, Printful, AliExpress (you apply as a platform partner - they love this because you bring them volume) OAuth integrations with Shopify and WooCommerce (so users connect their stores with one click) A webhook listener to catch orders and auto-forward to suppliers A product sync service that keeps prices/inventory updated This is a legit business model too - you can take a small margin on each sale or charge a monthly subscription. 1. AliExpress DS API Available Methods: Method Purpose Auth Required aliexpress.ds.product.search Search products by keyword/category app_key + sign aliexpress.ds.product.get Full product details, variants, images app_key + sign aliexpress.ds.category.get Get category tree app_key + sign aliexpress.ds.logistics.calculate Shipping costs per country app_key + sign aliexpress.ds.order.create Place dropship orders session token aliexpress.ds.order.get Query order status session token aliexpress.ds.order.tracking.get Tracking numbers session token aliexpress.ds.feedname.get Product feeds/recommendations app_key + sign aliexpress.ds.image.search Search by image app_key + sign aliexpress.ds.member.get Account info session token Data Available: Product title, images, price, original price, sale price, ratings, order volume, category, shipping options, variants with SKU/price/stock, delivery estimates.
2. CJ Dropshipping API v2.0 Endpoints: Endpoint Purpose POST /v1/product/list Search products POST /v1/product/query Product details by ID GET /v1/product/variant/queryByPid Get variants GET /v1/product/variant/queryByVid Variant by ID GET /v1/product/stock/queryByVid Real-time stock POST /v1/product/publish/listing Publish product POST /v1/logistic/freightCalculate Shipping costs GET /v1/logistic/getTrackInfo Tracking info POST /v1/shopping/order/batchCreateOrder Create orders GET /v1/shopping/order/queryById Order details POST /v1/shopping/order/confirm Confirm order GET /v1/shopping/pay/getBalance Account balance Data Available: Product name, images, sell price, shipping price, logistics days, category, variants, real-time stock levels, shipping calculations per country.
3. Printful API v2 Key Endpoints: Endpoint Purpose GET /v2/catalog-products List all products with filtering GET /v2/catalog-products/{id}/catalog-variants Product variants GET /v2/catalog-products/{id}/prices Actual pricing GET /v2/catalog-variants/{id}/prices Variant-level pricing GET /v2/catalog-products/{id}/availability Stock status GET /v2/catalog-products/{id}/images Product images GET /v2/catalog-categories Category listing GET /v2/catalog-products/{id}/mockup-styles Mockup styles POST /v2/mockup-tasks Generate mockups POST /v2/shipping-rates Calculate shipping POST /v2/orders Create orders GET /v2/orders/{id} Order details GET /v2/shipments Shipment tracking POST /v2/files Upload design files Data Available: Full catalog with categories, variant-level pricing (not hardcoded!), stock availability with 5-min refresh, mockup generation, shipping rate calculation, size guides.
4. Printify API Key Endpoints: Endpoint Purpose GET /v1/catalog/blueprints.json All product types GET /v1/catalog/blueprints/{id}.json Blueprint details GET /v1/catalog/blueprints/{id}/print_providers.json Compare providers GET /v1/catalog/blueprints/{id}/print_providers/{id}/variants.json Variants + pricing GET /v1/catalog/blueprints/{id}/print_providers/{id}/shipping.json Shipping rates GET /v1/catalog/print_providers.json All print providers POST /v1/shops/{id}/products.json Create product POST /v1/shops/{id}/products/{id}/publish.json Publish product POST /v1/shops/{id}/orders.json Create order Rate Limits: 600 req/min global, 100 req/min for catalog. Data Available: Blueprints (product types), multiple print providers per product with price comparison, variant-level pricing, shipping rates per provider, product creation/publishing.
5. Gooten API Key Endpoints: Endpoint Purpose GET /products Product catalog GET /productvariants Variants with pricing GET /shippingprices Shipping rates POST /price Order price estimate POST /orders Submit orders GET /orders Order details + tracking PUT /shippingAddress Update shipping GET /orderbilling Billing breakdown Auth: RecipeID in URL params. Data Available: Products, variants, country-specific pricing, shipping rates (standard/expedited/overnight), order cost estimates, tracking. Now let me fix the category browsing and improve the integration based on this research. Great question. For a $19.99/mo product where you want fast and seamless, here's the best approach: Recommended: Pay first, account auto-created Flow: User taps "Get Started" on homepage Goes straight to Stripe Checkout (hosted payment page) Stripe collects their email + card in one step (also supports Apple Pay / Google Pay) After payment, Stripe webhook fires → automatically creates their Supabase account User is redirected back to your app, already logged in They get a welcome email with a link to set their password (optional, for future logins) Why this is best: One step — no signup form, no password to think of, just pay and go Stripe is trusted — people are comfortable entering card details on Stripe's hosted page Apple Pay / Google Pay — literally one tap on mobile No abandoned signups — you only get paying customers, no dead free accounts Stripe handles PCI compliance — you never touch card numbers For returning users: They log in with email + password (or magic link) as normal Their Stripe subscription is linked to their Supabase account via stripe_customer_id vs Sign up first then pay: Two steps = more friction = lower conversion You end up with free accounts that never pay More code to manage the "signed up but not paid" state Would you like me to implement the Stripe Checkout integration with this flow? Great questions. Let me break this down: WooCommerce API — Yes, it has a full REST API. You can programmatically: Create products, update inventory, manage orders Set up shipping, taxes, coupons Manage customers and their accounts Sync everything back to ToGoGo Can the setup be automated? Mostly yes, here's the realistic path: Hosting — You'd use a hosting provider with an API (like Cloudways, RunCloud, or even spin up WordPress instances on a VPS via the WordPress CLI). When a user clicks "Set up my store," your backend provisions a WordPress instance automatically. WooCommerce install — WordPress CLI (wp-cli) can install WordPress + WooCommerce plugin in one command, fully automated. No manual work. Domain/URL — You could give users a subdomain like theirstore.togogo.me to start (free, instant), then let them connect a custom domain later (like Shopify does). WooCommerce REST API — Once the store exists, you use the WC REST API with consumer key/secret to push products, sync orders, etc. All automated. The business model fits nicely: $19.99/mo (current plan) — ToGoGo platform, marketing, suppliers, marketplace listings $29.99-49.99/mo (higher tier) — All the above + your own WooCommerce store hosted & managed by ToGoGo (your cost would be ~$5-10/mo per store for hosting) What you'd need to build: A provisioning service (create WordPress + WooCommerce instances) DNS management for subdomains (*.togogo.me) WooCommerce API integration to sync products from your suppliers This is absolutely doable and is essentially what Shopify charges $39+/mo for — you'd be undercutting them while giving users more flexibility. Fixed and pushed. The issue was in getStoreSubdomain() in src/App.jsx:54. The ?store=mystore query parameter was being checked after the early return for main hosts (togogo.me, www.togogo.me, etc.), so it was never reached on the production domain. The fix moves the ?store= query parameter check to the top of the function so it's evaluated first, before any host-based checks. I found the issue. There's a bug in the redirect URI construction in both google.js and callback.js. The NEXT_PUBLIC_URL variable (a Next.js convention) likely isn't set in this Vite project, and VERCEL_URL gives the deployment URL (like togogo-abc123.vercel.app) instead of the custom domain togogo.me. This causes a redirect URI mismatch with what's registered in Google OAuth console. The fix: use FRONTEND_URL (which is set to https://togogo.me) consistently for the OAuth redirect URI.

Here's what was wrong and what I fixed: The Bug: In both api/auth/google.js and api/auth/google/callback.js, the redirect URI was built using NEXT_PUBLIC_URL (a Next.js env var that doesn't exist in this Vite project). This caused a redirect URI mismatch with what's registered in your Google OAuth console. The Fix: Both files now use FRONTEND_URL (which is set to https://togogo.me) as the primary source for building the OAuth redirect URI. An error occurred while processing git_repository source. You can try again by sending a new message or starting a new session. An error occurred while processing git_repository source. You can try again by sending a new message or starting a new session. Great questions. Based on a thorough review of your codebase, here are the answers:
1. Does it get added to your database? Yes. Your webhook handler at api/webhooks/stripe.js processes several events that write to your database: customer.subscription.created — Inserts a record into the subscriptions table (user_id, plan, status, stripe_subscription_id, price_per_month, started_at, expires_at) checkout.session.completed — Updates user_stores status to 'paid' User's role gets upgraded from 'buyer' to 'subscriber' So after a successful checkout, you'll have records in both the subscriptions table and user_stores table.
2. Will it automatically charge monthly? Yes. Your checkout session in api/subscriptions/checkout.js uses mode: 'subscription', which means Stripe handles recurring billing automatically. Here's how it works: Stripe charges the customer monthly on the billing cycle date On success, Stripe fires invoice.payment_succeeded → your webhook updates expires_at to extend the subscription period On failure, Stripe fires invoice.payment_failed → your webhook marks the subscription as 'cancelled' If the customer cancels, Stripe fires customer.subscription.deleted → your webhook marks it 'expired' and downgrades the user role back to 'buyer' You don't need to do anything — Stripe manages the recurring charges, retries on failed payments, and sends you webhooks for each event.
3. Things to be aware of / study Here are the key concerns: Already handled well: Webhook signature verification (in production) Subscription lifecycle events (created, updated, deleted, invoice success/failure) User role management tied to subscription status Things to watch out for: Failed payment retries — Stripe retries failed invoices (default: 4 attempts over ~3 weeks). Your webhook currently marks the subscription as 'cancelled' on the first invoice.payment_failed. You may want to use a 'past_due' status instead and only cancel after all retries are exhausted (check the attempt_count on the invoice). Dunning emails — Configure Stripe's Smart Retries and dunning emails in your Stripe Dashboard (Settings → Billing → Subscriptions) so customers get notified about failed payments before cancellation. Customer portal — Consider adding Stripe's Customer Portal so users can self-manage their subscription (update payment method, cancel, view invoices). This is a simple redirect and saves you support work. Proration on plan changes — If users upgrade/downgrade between plans, make sure your customer.subscription.updated webhook handles proration correctly. Webhook reliability — In dev mode, your webhook bypasses signature verification (which is fine for testing). Just make sure STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET is always set in production. Subscription state sync — If a webhook is missed (rare but possible), your DB could get out of sync with Stripe. Consider adding a periodic sync job or a "verify with Stripe" check when users access subscription-gated features. Tax collection — Since you're billing in AUD, you may need to collect GST. Stripe Tax can automate this — worth investigating for compliance. Would you like me to implement any of these improvements (like the past_due status handling or adding a customer portal endpoint)? Please implement or seven, thank you Claude

I found the problem. There are two bugs causing Stuart's store to not show up: Bug 1: sessionStorage lost during Stripe redirect. When Stuart pays on Stripe and gets redirected back, the code checks sessionStorage.getItem('togogo-deploy-active'). On mobile browsers (and sometimes desktop), sessionStorage is cleared during cross-domain redirects. If that's null, the payment success handler never fires, the activate endpoint is never called, and the store stays stuck in 'pending' or 'provisioning' status. Bug 2: The activate endpoint doesn't upgrade the user role or ensure a subscription exists. Even when it does run, it only sets user_stores.status = 'active' — it doesn't upgrade the user from 'buyer' to 'subscriber' or create a subscription record. Let me also check if STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET is likely missing (which would mean the webhook is rejected in production).
